SHOW SUMMARY:

The Opie and Anthony Show broadcast covered a wide range of topics, often shifting rapidly between segments and caller interactions.  The show opened with Anthony detailing his recent, financially devastating divorce, revealing his ex-wife emptied their joint account, leaving him with only $42.  He lamented the perceived unfairness of divorce laws, alongside humorous anecdotes about his disastrous morning commute in his girlfriend's car (featuring inescapable Gwen Stefani music) and a subsequent gas station mishap.  His extreme dislike of children was a recurring theme, fueled by stories involving his girlfriend's family and a child's booger-on-the-couch incident that resulted in the couch's disposal.  Listener calls, promotional material for XM Satellite Radio, and contributions from E-Rock, Danny, Nathaniel, and Travis punctuated this segment.

The show then transitioned into a chaotic mix of segments.  Nonsensical chatter between Opie and Anthony led to brief calls from Tom in Philly and Mike in Kansas, the latter featuring a humorous booger-in-the-couch anecdote mirroring Anthony's earlier story.  A listener-submitted song parody, using homophobic slurs, mocked Martini Steve and his hybrid car.  This was followed by a segment where the hosts and a studio guest, Steve, cleaned up listener-submitted audio clips for television broadcast, replacing profanity with euphemisms and altering lines for comedic effect.  The original and cleaned-up versions of these extremely vulgar clips (containing graphic sexual references and homophobic slurs) were played.  A clip from a 1950s film warning about pornography's effects on youth was satirized with crude jokes.  Regis Philbin's singing career became a target for crude, sexually explicit improvisational lyrics.  Calls from Krista (a blind listener) and Jay in Cleveland (who was subjected to intense homophobic ribbing) followed.  The segment concluded with a vulgar negotiation with Patty, a listener who'd sent disliked Christmas presents, resulting in Patty flashing her underwear on air for additional payment after the hosts sold her gifts on eBay for $770.

A "Let's Make a Deal" game with Patty saw her win $770 for a series of increasingly bizarre challenges involving nudity, a Crusty the Clown mask, a tarp, apples, KY jelly, and a "cherry dart" game.  Several interns witnessed Patty's naked crawl across the studio.  Opie shared stories about a near-fire incident caused by "java logs" and a low-blood-sugar meltdown requiring milk retrieval from a Dwayne Reed store by Ricky, greatly amusing Anthony. The show then played listener-submitted remixes of Pat O’Brien’s leaked sexually explicit voicemails, detailing the scandal, including alleged derogatory comments towards a coworker and flirtation attempts with Oprah Winfrey. This segment also featured a drunken on-air appearance by Frankie Blue (program director of WNEW), highlighting his incoherence and unprofessional behavior, ultimately ending with audio of his firing.

A caller recounted explicit childhood sexual experiences, including encounters with overweight women and a developmentally disabled girl, described with offensive language. This was followed by a highly critical and vulgar discussion of Tara Reid's "Taradice" travel show, featuring impressions and commentary on Reid's appearance and speech, punctuated by audio clips. Comedian Bob Kelly was a guest during this segment.

The "Bombs and Flubs" segment highlighted Jimmy Norton's failed jokes (including those about Y2K, sex with an elderly woman, and sex with a paralyzed woman), while Anthony Cumia had no flubs.  Past flubs were also reviewed, along with a call from John and Al, creators of a *Silence of the Lambs* parody musical.  Howie Mandel’s potty-training anecdote involving a ravine and urination was recounted, along with a news story about an 86-year-old woman repeatedly calling 911 about pizza delivery, featuring Dee Dee's distinctive accent.  Debbie Gibson's and Tiffany's Playboy spreads were compared, and a caller shared a story about stealing and viewing porn from vending machines in a tree fort.

A rambling discussion with Jimmy Robinson included childhood reminiscences (building tree forts and attempting to form the disastrously named "The Lords" gang), explicit discussions about pornography, and Jimmy's injury from a falling studio panel.  A heated exchange with "Dragon Wagon," a long-haul trucker offended by the show's content, ensued.  Bernie, an in-studio guest with *Weekly World News*, became upset when Opie switched his CD, briefly leaving the studio.

Bernie’s subsequent enraged departure, compared to Dustin Hoffman in *Rain Man*, was followed by a call with comedian Rich Voss, who recounted answering a phone call from his girlfriend mid-comedy performance, leading to teasing about his being "pussy-whipped." A guest’s visit, resulting in broken poker chips and a hat box, caused a further upset departure, met with laughter from the hosts. Billy Burr was mentioned as a guest, but didn’t feature in this specific segment.  Joe Rogan’s material was previewed.

A segment featured hockey highlights, a listener-submitted volatile father-son argument filled with profanity, and Big A's flawed karaoke performances of "Waiting for a Girl Like You" and "Brown Eyed Girl."  A phone call from Bob Kelly and a highly profane remote with John Valby at Steinway piano headquarters, resulting in uncomfortable interactions with staff, were also included.  A "terror tape" was briefly discussed.

The show discussed old, racist cigarette commercials (featuring the Flintstones), classic cartoons, and Opie's smoking habits (following a call from Peter from WhackBag.com).  The hosts’ racist and sexist commentary accompanied the playing of vintage cigarette ads.  A call from John from Jersey offered compliments.  A bizarre event involving "Tippi Tom," a sleeping homeless man outside the studio, resulted in a chaotic and profanity-laced interaction.  Celine Dion's post-Hurricane Katrina appearance on Larry King Live was mocked with offensive jokes.

The show covered the Discovery Channel's "Deadliest Catch," described as a "crab holocaust," with an extended playing of Gordon Lightfoot's "The Wreck of the Edmund Fitzgerald."  A caller who was a commercial fisherman defended the crab fishermen.  A prank call segment targeting the Tony Danza Show, featuring Anthony's Tony Danza impression, resulted in explicit promises and a team member's arrest for disorderly conduct.

A post-interview discussion about Eric's cell phone being knocked from his hand during an interview, possibly due to mistaken identity with Z100, was followed by a visit from Bob Saget, who recounted crude and sexually explicit anecdotes.  A caller criticized Dave Coulier, prompting Saget’s defense.  Charles Ross, a one-man Star Wars show performer, had a disrupted interview due to inappropriate calls from "Steve from Yellowstone," ultimately leaving before the interview concluded.

A call-in segment with Charles, discussing Star Wars and his One Man Lord of the Rings show, was punctuated by numerous calls from Steve, who repeatedly shouted "Ramone!" and made offensive statements.  Other callers praised Charles's knowledge or participated in the "Ramone" calls.  An excerpt from Charles’s show and a promotion for a "best of" compilation concluded the segment.
